{"type":"response.output_text.done","content_index":0,"item_id":"msg_03b7acbb1fb030660169c2c8f5a8c481939536127e5cdbbe72","logprobs":[],"output_index":0,"sequence_number":700,"text":"Here’s a concise summary of the most important algorithms and data structures from your documentation that every developer should know.\n\n## Core data structures\n\n- **Arrays**\n  - Best for indexed access.\n  - Common operations: get, set, push, pop, insert, remove.\n  - Know tradeoffs for insertion/removal in the middle.\n\n- **Linked Lists**\n  - Useful when frequent insertions/removals matter more than random access.\n  - Know append, prepend, find, remove, toArray.\n\n- **Stacks**\n  - LIFO structure.\n  - Common uses: undo/redo, browser history, call stack, DFS.\n\n- **Queues**\n  - FIFO structure.\n  - Common uses: task processing, BFS, request handling.\n\n- **Priority Queues / Heaps**\n  - Useful when you repeatedly need the highest/lowest priority item.\n  - Important for schedulers and graph algorithms like Dijkstra.\n\n- **Hash Tables**\n  - Fast average-case lookup, insertion, deletion.\n  - Fundamental for dictionaries, caches, frequency counting, indexing.\n\n- **Trees**\n  - Especially **Binary Search Trees**.\n  - Important concepts: insert, find, traversals, height, min, max.\n\n- **Graphs**\n  - Essential for modeling networks, dependencies, routes, relationships.\n  - Know adjacency lists, DFS, BFS, shortest path.\n\n## Core algorithms\n\n- **Searching**\n  - **Linear Search**: simple, works on unsorted data.\n  - **Binary Search**: fast lookup on sorted arrays.\n\n- **Sorting**\n  - **Quick Sort**: fast in practice, divide and conquer.\n  - **Merge Sort**: stable and reliable O(n log n).\n  - **Heap Sort**: useful when working with heaps.\n\n- **Graph Traversal**\n  - **DFS (Depth-First Search)**: useful for traversal, recursion-style problems.\n  - **BFS (Breadth-First Search)**: useful for shortest path in unweighted graphs.\n\n- **Shortest Path**\n  - **Dijkstra’s Algorithm** for weighted graphs with non-negative edges.\n\n- **Dynamic Programming**\n  - Key mindset: break big problems into overlapping subproblems.\n  - Must-know examples:\n    - Fibonacci\n    - Longest Common Subsequence\n    - Knapsack\n    - Coin Change\n    - Edit Distance\n\n## Supporting fundamentals\n\n- **Big O notation**\n  - You should understand:\n    - O(1)\n    - O(log n)\n    - O(n)\n    - O(n log n)\n    - O(n²)\n    - O(2^n)\n    - O(n!)\n\n## What matters most in practice\n\nIf you prioritize, focus on these first:\n\n1. Arrays\n2. Hash tables\n3. Stacks and queues\n4. Trees\n5. Graphs\n6. Binary search\n7. DFS and BFS\n8. Quick sort / Merge sort\n9. Heaps / priority queues\n10. Dynamic programming basics\n\n## Simple takeaway\n\nEvery developer should be comfortable with:\n- storing data efficiently,\n- searching and sorting it,\n- traversing trees and graphs,\n- and reasoning about time complexity.\n\nIf you want, I can turn this into:\n1. a **beginner-friendly study roadmap**,\n2. a **cheat sheet table**, or\n3. a **JavaScript-focused version with code examples**."}

Best for indexed access.\n  - Common operations: get, set, push, pop, insert, remove.\n  - Know tradeoffs for insertion/removal in the middle.\n\n- **Linked Lists**\n  - Useful when frequent insertions/removals matter more than random access.\n  - Know append, prepend, find, remove, toArray.\n\n- **Stacks**\n  - LIFO structure.\n  - Common uses: undo/redo, browser history, call stack, DFS.\n\n- **Queues**\n  - FIFO structure.\n  - Common uses: task processing, BFS, request handling.\n\n- **Priority Queues / Heaps**\n  - Useful when you repeatedly need the highest/lowest priority item.\n  - Important for schedulers and graph algorithms like Dijkstra.\n\n- **Hash Tables**\n  - Fast average-case lookup, insertion, deletion.\n  - Fundamental for dictionaries, caches, frequency counting, indexing.\n\n- **Trees**\n  - Especially **Binary Search Trees**.\n  - Important concepts: insert, find, traversals, height, min, max.\n\n- **Graphs**\n  - Essential for modeling networks, dependencies, routes, relationships.\n  - Know adjacency lists, DFS, BFS, shortest path.\n\n## Core algorithms\n\n- **Searching**\n  - **Linear Search**: simple, works on unsorted data.\n  - **Binary Search**: fast lookup on sorted arrays.\n\n- **Sorting**\n  - **Quick Sort**: fast in practice, divide and conquer.\n  - **Merge Sort**: stable and reliable O(n log n).\n  - **Heap Sort**: useful when working with heaps.\n\n- **Graph Traversal**\n  - **DFS (Depth-First Search)**: useful for traversal, recursion-style problems.\n  - **BFS (Breadth-First Search)**: useful for shortest path in unweighted graphs.\n\n- **Shortest Path**\n  - **Dijkstra’s Algorithm** for weighted graphs with non-negative edges.\n\n- **Dynamic Programming**\n  - Key mindset: break big problems into overlapping subproblems.\n  - Must-know examples:\n    - Fibonacci\n    - Longest Common Subsequence\n    - Knapsack\n    - Coin Change\n    - Edit Distance\n\n## Supporting fundamentals\n\n- **Big O notation**\n  - You should understand:\n    - O(1)\n    - O(log n)\n    - O(n)\n    - O(n log n)\n    - O(n²)\n    - O(2^n)\n    - O(n!)\n\n## What matters most in practice\n\nIf you prioritize, focus on these first:\n\n1. Arrays\n2. Hash tables\n3. Stacks and queues\n4. Trees\n5. Graphs\n6. Binary search\n7. DFS and BFS\n8. Quick sort / Merge sort\n9. Heaps / priority queues\n10.
